{=Wells, Somerset=}\n

documents on fol. 14r in a somewhat later kind of language=}\n

# 173\n
{Worcester Cathedral, Chapter Library F 174, fols. 1r-63r: AElfric\'s Grammar and Glossary}\n
C13a\n
384 254 E\n
{=Worcester, Worcs=}\n
{=Sample represents all the legible bits of English in this text only\n
in the same hand (the Worcester Tremulous Hand), as the Worcester\n
Fragments (text no. 172 worcthfragst.tag) and the Nicene Creed (text no.\n
171 worcthcreedt.tag) which have been tagged separately because the\n
language is slightly different, that of the Grammar and Glossary being\n
influenced by being copied from an Old English original=}\n
{=Script - Textura semiquadrata. The hand has a characteristic leftward\n
slant, is variable in size, regularity and in degree of tremor=}\n
{=Status - complex commentary, adding of Latin text for context and\n
punctuation done up to the end of f28v so far=}\n
{=The manuscript is composed of sheets of different sizes most of\n
which are incomplete having been cut up in C15 and pasted together\n
for use as bindings. The manuscript was reconstituted in C19 but\n
fol. 10 belongs between fols. 1 and 2. For this tagged text I have\n
placed it as fol. 2 in the correct order for the text and renumbered all\n
subsequent folios accordingly. All the fol. references in the tagged\n
text apart from fols. 1 and 2 will have a number one more than their\n
actual place in the manuscript. As a result of its history, the\n
manuscript is in poor condition with the edges cropped and\n
considerable text lost also as a result of the paste used on it\n
and the subsequent washing off of the paste. Since I have worked\n
with a microfilm it is likely that the problems of legibility are\n
worse than they would have been using the original. I have only\n
tagged complete or almost complete words. Original presence of what\n
is now illegible or missing text is noted within braces and square\n
brackets according to usual practice. Supplied words are not\n
reconstructions but are modern English equivalents of the conjectured\n
text given to aid comprehension. The same applies to such of the\n
Latin text I have been able to decipher. I have tried to put in\n
as much of the Latin as possible because it is necessary for the\n
understanding of the context of much of the English=}\n
{~f1r~}\n
{=Begins imperfectly - the preface and the first few lines of the\n
grammar itself are lost. This first folio is also much rubbed with\n
inevitable loss of legibility=}\n

# 172\n
{Worcester Cathedral, Chapter Library F 174, fols. 63r-66v: Worcester Fragments}\n
C13a\n
384 254 N\n
{=Worcester, Worcs=}\n
{=Sample consists of this text only, in the same hand (the Worcester\n
Tremulous Hand), as his version of Aelfric\'s Grammar and Glossary (see\n
text no. 173 worcthgrglt.tag) and the Nicene Creed (text no. 171\n
worcthcreedt.tag) which have been tagged separately because the language\n
is slightly different, that of the Grammar and Glossary being influenced\n
by being copied from an Old English original=}\n
{=Script - Textura semiquadrata. The hand has a characteristic leftward\n
slant, is variable in size, regularity and in degree of tremor=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=The manuscript is composed of sheets of different sizes most of which\n
are incomplete having been cut up in C15 and pasted together for use as\n
bindings. The manuscript was reconstituted in C19 but is in poor condition\n
with the edges cropped and considerable text lost also as a result of the\n
paste used on it and the subsequent washing off of the paste. Since I have\n
worked with a microfilm rather than the original manuscript it is likely\n
that the problems of legibility are worse than they would have been using\n
the original. I have only tagged complete or almost complete words. The\n
manuscript has been cropped at the top leading to loss of text at the\n
beginning of each side of each folio. The resulting fragments are here\n
treated as separate texts. The first is part of a poem on the disuse of\n
English. The following seven are all fragments of the same poem, a version\n
of the Soul\'s Address to the Body. The MS has also been cropped on the\n
outer edge with the loss of probably 3 or 4 letters at the end of each\n
line of the rectos and beginning of each line of the versos. The corner\n
near the bound edge is also damaged with some loss to the last lines of\n
each side. The words supplied in square brackets in lower case are to\n
aid comprehension and do not attempt to supply MS readings. They are derived\n
from a consensus of suggested readings that have been supplied by other editors=}\n
{~f63r~}\n
